   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Laos</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Landlocked country in Southeast Asia
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Laon" title="Laon">Laon</a>.
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       This article is about the country in Southeast Asia. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Laos_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Laos (disambiguation)">Laos (disambiguation)</a>.
      </div>

      <p><b>Laos</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Laos.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/69/En-us-Laos.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Laos.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/aʊ/: 'ou' in 'mouth'">aʊ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span><span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lao_language" title="Lao language">Lao</a>: <span lang="lo">ລາວ</span>, <i>Lāo</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Lao" title="Help:IPA/Lao">[láːw]</a></span>), officially the <b>Lao People's Democratic Republic</b> (<a href="/wiki/Lao_language" title="Lao language">Lao</a>: <span lang="lo" title="Lao-language text">ສາທາລະນະລັດ ປະຊາທິປະໄຕ ປະຊາຊົນລາວ</span>, <i>Sathalanalat Paxathipatai Paxaxôn Lao</i>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">République démocratique populaire lao</i>), is a <a href="/wiki/Socialist_state" title="Socialist state">socialist state</a> and the only <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a> in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>. At the heart of the <a href="/wiki/Mainland_Southeast_Asia" title="Mainland Southeast Asia">Indochinese Peninsula</a>, Laos is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a> and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> to the northwest, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> to the east, <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a> to the southeast and <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> to the west and southwest.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Present Laos traces its historic and cultural identity to <a href="/wiki/Lan_Xang" title="Lan Xang">Lan Xang</a>, which existed from the 14th century to the 18th century as one of the largest kingdoms in Southeast Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-Stuart-Fox_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stuart-Fox-12">[12]</a></sup> Because of its central geographical location in Southeast Asia, the kingdom became a hub for overland trade and became wealthy economically and culturally.<sup id="cite_ref-Stuart-Fox_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stuart-Fox-12">[12]</a></sup> After a period of internal conflict, Lan Xang broke into three separate kingdoms—<a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Luang_Phrabang" title="Kingdom of Luang Phrabang">Luang Phrabang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Vientiane" title="Kingdom of Vientiane">Vientiane</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Champasak" title="Kingdom of Champasak">Champasak</a>. In 1893, the three territories came under a <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">French protectorate</a> and were united to form what is now known as Laos. It briefly gained independence in 1945 after <a href="/wiki/History_of_Laos_to_1945#Japanese_occupation_of_Laos" class="mw-redirect" title="History of Laos to 1945">Japanese occupation</a> but was recolonised by <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> until it won autonomy in 1949. Laos became independent in 1953, with a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> under <a href="/wiki/Sisavang_Vong" title="Sisavang Vong">Sisavang Vong</a>. A post-independence <a href="/wiki/Laotian_Civil_War" title="Laotian Civil War">civil war</a> began, which saw the <a href="/wiki/Lao_People%27s_Revolutionary_Party" title="Lao People's Revolutionary Party">communist resistance</a>, supported by the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, fight against the monarchy that later came under influence of military regimes supported by the United States. After the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> ended in 1975, the <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">communist</a> <a href="/wiki/Pathet_Lao" title="Pathet Lao">Pathet Lao</a> came to power, ending the civil war. Laos was then dependent on military and economic aid from the Soviet Union until its <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution</a> in 1991. </p>
      <p>Laos is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Asia-Pacific_Trade_Agreement" title="Asia-Pacific Trade Agreement">Asia-Pacific Trade Agreement</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations" class="mw-redirect" title="Association of Southeast Asian Nations">ASEAN</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Asia_Summit" title="East Asia Summit">East Asia Summit</a>, and <a href="/wiki/La_Francophonie" class="mw-redirect" title="La Francophonie">La Francophonie</a>. Laos applied for membership of the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> in 1997; on 2 February 2013, it was granted full membership.<sup id="cite_ref-wto_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wto-13">[13]</a></sup> It is a <a href="/wiki/One-party_state" title="One-party state">one-party</a> socialist republic, espousing <a href="/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism" title="Marxism–Leninism">Marxism–Leninism</a> governed by the <a href="/wiki/Lao_People%27s_Revolutionary_Party" title="Lao People's Revolutionary Party">Lao People's Revolutionary Party</a>. </p>
      <p>The politically and culturally dominant <a href="/wiki/Lao_people" title="Lao people">Lao people</a> make up 53.2% of the population, mostly in the lowlands. <a href="/wiki/Austroasiatic_languages" title="Austroasiatic languages">Mon-Khmer</a> groups, the <a href="/wiki/Hmong_people" title="Hmong people">Hmong</a>, and other indigenous hill tribes live in the foothills and mountains. Laos' strategies for development are based on <a href="/wiki/Electricity_generation" title="Electricity generation">generating electricity</a> from rivers and selling the power to its neighbours, namely Thailand, China, and Vietnam, as well as its initiative to become a "land-linked" nation, as evidenced by the <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Laos#Railways" title="Transport in Laos">construction of four new railways connecting Laos and neighbours</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbcdam_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcdam-15">[15]</a></sup> Laos has been referred to as one of Southeast Asia and Pacific's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_real_GDP_growth_rate" title="List of countries by real GDP growth rate">fastest growing economies</a> by the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> with annual GDP growth averaging 7.7% since 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-17">[17]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading">
       <input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none">

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The English word <i>Laos</i> was coined by the <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">French</a>, who united the three Lao kingdoms in <a href="/wiki/French_Indochina" title="French Indochina">French Indochina</a> in 1893 and named the country as the plural of the dominant and most common ethnic group, the <a href="/wiki/Lao_people" title="Lao people">Lao people</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tripsavvy_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tripsavvy-18">[18]</a></sup> English speakers often mispronounce the word 'Laos', falsely believing that it should be pronounced with a silent 's', however the 's' in Laos should not be silent.<sup id="cite_ref-tripsavvy_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tripsavvy-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fodors_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fodors-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Lao_language" title="Lao language">Lao language</a>, the country's name is <i><a href="/wiki/Mueang#Laos" title="Mueang">Muang Lao</a></i> (<span lang="lo" title="Lao-language text">ເມືອງລາວ</span>) or <i>Pathet Lao</i> (<span lang="lo" title="Lao-language text">ປະເທດລາວ</span>), both of which literally mean 'Lao Country'.<sup id="cite_ref-Kislenko2009_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kislenko2009-23">[23]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Laos" title="History of Laos">History of Laos</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pha_That_Luang,_Vientiane,_Laos.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Pha_That_Luang%2C_Vientiane%2C_Laos.jpg/220px-Pha_That_Luang%2C_Vientiane%2C_Laos.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Pha_That_Luang%2C_Vientiane%2C_Laos.jpg/330px-Pha_That_Luang%2C_Vientiane%2C_Laos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Pha_That_Luang%2C_Vientiane%2C_Laos.jpg/440px-Pha_That_Luang%2C_Vientiane%2C_Laos.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="664"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pha_That_Luang,_Vientiane,_Laos.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Pha_That_Luang" title="Pha That Luang">Pha That Luang</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vientiane" title="Vientiane">Vientiane</a> is the national symbol of Laos.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>An ancient human skull was recovered in 2009 from the <a href="/wiki/Tam_Pa_Ling_Cave" title="Tam Pa Ling Cave">Tam Pa Ling Cave</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Annamite_Range" title="Annamite Range">Annamite Mountains</a> in northern Laos; the skull is at least 46,000 years old, making it the oldest modern human fossil found to date in Southeast Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Stone artifacts including <a href="/wiki/Hoabinhian" title="Hoabinhian">Hoabinhian</a> types have been found at sites dating to the Late <a href="/wiki/Pleistocene" title="Pleistocene">Pleistocene</a> in northern Laos.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Archaeological evidence suggests an agriculturist society developed during the 4th millennium BC.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Burial jars and other kinds of sepulchers suggest a complex society in which bronze objects appeared around 1500 BC, and iron tools were known from 700 BC. The proto-historic period is characterised by contact with Chinese and Indian civilisations. According to linguistic and other historical evidence, <a href="/wiki/Tai_languages" title="Tai languages">Tai-speaking</a> tribes migrated southwestward to the modern territories of Laos and Thailand from <a href="/wiki/Guangxi" title="Guangxi">Guangxi</a> sometime between the 8th and 10th centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-PittayawatPittayaporn_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PittayawatPittayaporn-27">[27]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lan_Xang">Lan Xang</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Lan Xang">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lan_Xang" title="Lan Xang">Lan Xang</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Fa_Ngum-Vtne1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Fa_Ngum-Vtne1.JPG/170px-Fa_Ngum-Vtne1.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="241" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Fa_Ngum-Vtne1.JPG/255px-Fa_Ngum-Vtne1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Fa_Ngum-Vtne1.JPG/340px-Fa_Ngum-Vtne1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2110" data-file-height="2996"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Fa_Ngum-Vtne1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Fa_Ngum" title="Fa Ngum">Fa Ngum</a>, founder of the <a href="/wiki/Lan_Xang" title="Lan Xang">Lan Xang</a> Kingdom
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Laos traces its history to the kingdom of Lan Xang ('million elephants'), which was founded in the 14th century by a Lao prince, <a href="/wiki/Fa_Ngum" title="Fa Ngum">Fa Ngum</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Coedes_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coedes-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>223</span></sup> whose father had his family exiled from the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Empire" title="Khmer Empire">Khmer Empire</a>. Fa Ngum, with 10,000 <a href="/wiki/Khmer_people" title="Khmer people">Khmer</a> troops, conquered many Lao principalities in the <a href="/wiki/Mekong" title="Mekong">Mekong</a> river basin, culminating in the capture of <a href="/wiki/Vientiane" title="Vientiane">Vientiane</a>. Ngum was descended from a long line of Lao kings that traced back to Khoun Boulom.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> He made <a href="/wiki/Theravada" title="Theravada">Theravada Buddhism</a> the state religion, and Lan Xang prospered. His ministers, unable to tolerate his ruthlessness, forced him into exile to the present-day Thai province of <a href="/wiki/Nan_Province" title="Nan Province">Nan</a> in 1373,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> where he died. Fa Ngum's eldest son, Oun Heuan, ascended to the throne under the name <a href="/wiki/Samsenethai" title="Samsenethai">Samsenethai</a> and reigned for 43&nbsp;years. Lan Xang became an important trade centre during Samsenthai's reign, but after his death in 1421 it collapsed into warring factions for nearly a century.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1520, <a href="/wiki/Photisarath" title="Photisarath">Photisarath</a> came to the throne and moved the capital from <a href="/wiki/Luang_Prabang" title="Luang Prabang">Luang Prabang</a> to Vientiane to avoid a Burmese invasion. <a href="/wiki/Setthathirath" title="Setthathirath">Setthathirath</a> became king in 1548, after his father was killed, and ordered the construction of what became the symbol of Laos, <a href="/wiki/Pha_That_Luang" title="Pha That Luang">That Luang</a>. Settathirath disappeared in the mountains on his way back from a military expedition into Cambodia, and Lan Xang fell into more than seventy years of instability, involving both Burmese invasion and civil war.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1637, when <a href="/wiki/Sourigna_Vongsa" title="Sourigna Vongsa">Sourigna Vongsa</a> ascended the throne, Lan Xang further expanded its frontiers. His reign is often regarded as Laos's golden age. When he died without an heir, the kingdom split into three principalities. Between 1763 and 1769, Burmese armies overran northern Laos and annexed <a href="/wiki/Luang_Prabang" title="Luang Prabang">Luang Prabang</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Champasak" title="Kingdom of Champasak">Champasak</a> eventually came under <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Siamese</a> <a href="/wiki/Suzerainty" title="Suzerainty">suzerainty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Anouvong" title="Anouvong">Chao Anouvong</a> was installed as a vassal king of Vientiane by the Siamese. He encouraged a renaissance of Lao fine arts and literature and improved relations with Luang Phrabang. Under Vietnamese pressure, <a href="/wiki/Lao_rebellion_(1826%E2%80%931828)" title="Lao rebellion (1826–1828)">he rebelled against the Siamese in 1826</a>. The rebellion failed, and Vientiane was ransacked.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Anouvong was taken to <a href="/wiki/Bangkok" title="Bangkok">Bangkok</a> as a prisoner, where he died.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A Siamese military campaign in Laos in 1876 was described by a British observer as having been "transformed into <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Asia" title="Slavery in Asia">slave-hunting raids</a> on a large scale".<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="French_Laos_.281893.E2.80.931953.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="French_Laos_(1893–1953)">French Laos (1893–1953)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: French Laos (1893–1953)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/French_protectorate_of_Laos" title="French protectorate of Laos">French protectorate of Laos</a> and <a href="/wiki/First_Indochina_War" title="First Indochina War">First Indochina War</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Local_Lao_in_the_French_Colonial_guard.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Local_Lao_in_the_French_Colonial_guard.png/220px-Local_Lao_in_the_French_Colonial_guard.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Local_Lao_in_the_French_Colonial_guard.png/330px-Local_Lao_in_the_French_Colonial_guard.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Local_Lao_in_the_French_Colonial_guard.png/440px-Local_Lao_in_the_French_Colonial_guard.png 2x" data-file-width="674" data-file-height="386"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Local_Lao_in_the_French_Colonial_guard.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Local Lao soldiers in the French Colonial guard, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1900</span>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the late 19th century, Luang Prabang was ransacked by the Chinese <a href="/wiki/Black_Flag_Army" title="Black Flag Army">Black Flag Army</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> France rescued King <a href="/wiki/Oun_Kham" title="Oun Kham">Oun Kham</a> and added Luang Phrabang to the protectorate of <a href="/wiki/French_Indochina" title="French Indochina">French Indochina</a>. Shortly after, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Champasak" title="Kingdom of Champasak">Kingdom of Champasak</a> and the territory of Vientiane were added to the protectorate. King <a href="/wiki/Sisavang_Vong" title="Sisavang Vong">Sisavang Vong</a> of Luang Phrabang became ruler of a unified Laos, and Vientiane once again became the capital.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Laos never held any importance for France<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> other than as a buffer state between Thailand and the more economically important <a href="/wiki/Annam_(French_protectorate)" title="Annam (French protectorate)">Annam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tonkin" title="Tonkin">Tonkin</a>. </p>
      <p>Laos produced <a href="/wiki/Tin" title="Tin">tin</a>, rubber, and coffee, but never accounted for more than one percent of French Indochina's exports. By 1940, around 600 French citizens lived in Laos.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Under French rule, the Vietnamese were encouraged to migrate to Laos, which was seen by the French colonists as a rational solution to a labour shortage within the confines of an Indochina-wide colonial space.<sup id="cite_ref-SørenIvarsson_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SørenIvarsson-41">[41]</a></sup> By 1943, the Vietnamese population stood at nearly 40,000, forming the majority in the largest cities of Laos and enjoying the right to elect its own leaders.<sup id="cite_ref-MartinStuart-FoxA_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MartinStuart-FoxA-42">[42]</a></sup> As a result, 53% of the population of Vientiane, 85% of <a href="/wiki/Thakhek" title="Thakhek">Thakhek</a>, and 62% of <a href="/wiki/Pakse" title="Pakse">Pakse</a> were Vietnamese, with only the exception of <a href="/wiki/Luang_Prabang" title="Luang Prabang">Luang Prabang</a> where the population was predominantly Lao.<sup id="cite_ref-MartinStuart-FoxA_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MartinStuart-FoxA-42">[42]</a></sup> As late as 1945, the French drew up an ambitious plan to move massive Vietnamese population to three key areas, i.e., the Vientiane Plain, <a href="/wiki/Savannakhet_Province" title="Savannakhet Province">Savannakhet region</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Bolaven_Plateau" title="Bolaven Plateau">Bolaven Plateau</a>, which was only derailed by the Japanese invasion of Indochina.<sup id="cite_ref-MartinStuart-FoxA_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MartinStuart-FoxA-42">[42]</a></sup> Otherwise, according to <a href="/wiki/Martin_Stuart-Fox" title="Martin Stuart-Fox">Martin Stuart-Fox</a>, the Lao might well have lost control over their own country.<sup id="cite_ref-MartinStuart-FoxA_42-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MartinStuart-FoxA-42">[42]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During <a href="/wiki/French_Protectorate_of_Laos#Laos_during_World_War_II" class="mw-redirect" title="French Protectorate of Laos">World War II in Laos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vichy_France" title="Vichy France">Vichy France</a>, Thailand, <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Imperial Japan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Free_France" title="Free France">Free France</a> occupied Laos.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> On 9 March 1945, a nationalist group declared Laos once more independent, with Luang Prabang as its capital, but on 7 April 1945 two battalions of Japanese troops occupied the city.<sup id="cite_ref-A_Country_Study:_Laos_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_Country_Study:_Laos-44">[44]</a></sup> The Japanese attempted to force <a href="/wiki/Sisavang_Vong" title="Sisavang Vong">Sisavang Vong</a> (the King of Luang Phrabang) to declare Laotian independence, but on 8 April he instead simply declared an end to Laos's status as a French protectorate. The king then secretly sent Prince <a href="/wiki/Kindavong" title="Kindavong">Kindavong</a> to represent Laos to the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied forces</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sisavang_Vatthana" title="Sisavang Vatthana">Prince Sisavang</a> as representative to the Japanese.<sup id="cite_ref-A_Country_Study:_Laos_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_Country_Study:_Laos-44">[44]</a></sup> When Japan surrendered, some Lao nationalists (including Prince <a href="/wiki/Phetsarath_Ratanavongsa" title="Phetsarath Ratanavongsa">Phetsarath</a>) declared Laotian independence, but by early-1946, French troops had reoccupied the country and conferred limited autonomy on Laos.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-45">[45]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/First_Indochina_War" title="First Indochina War">First Indochina War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Indochinese_Communist_Party" title="Indochinese Communist Party">Indochinese Communist Party</a> formed the <a href="/wiki/Pathet_Lao" title="Pathet Lao">Pathet Lao</a> independence organisation. The Pathet Lao began a war against the French colonial forces with the aid of the Vietnamese independence organisation, the <a href="/wiki/Viet_Minh" title="Viet Minh">Viet Minh</a>. In 1950, the French were forced to give Laos semi-autonomy as an "associated state" within the <a href="/wiki/French_Union" title="French Union">French Union</a>. France remained in de facto control until 22 October 1953, when Laos gained full independence as a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-britannica_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-45">[45]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Independence_and_Communist_rule_.281953.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_and_Communist_rule_(1953–present)">Independence and Communist rule (1953–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Independence and Communist rule (1953–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Laos_since_1945" title="History of Laos since 1945">History of Laos since 1945</a> and <a href="/wiki/Laotian_Civil_War" title="Laotian Civil War">Laotian Civil War</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:FrenchLaos1953.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/FrenchLaos1953.png/220px-FrenchLaos1953.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="197" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/FrenchLaos1953.png/330px-FrenchLaos1953.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/FrenchLaos1953.png/440px-FrenchLaos1953.png 2x" data-file-width="2517" data-file-height="2257"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:FrenchLaos1953.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>French <a href="/wiki/Raoul_Salan" title="Raoul Salan">General Salan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sisavang_Vatthana" title="Sisavang Vatthana">Prince Sisavang Vatthana</a> in Luang Prabang, 4 May 1953
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The First Indochina War took place across French Indochina and eventually led to French defeat and the signing of a peace accord for Laos at the <a href="/wiki/1954_Geneva_Conference" title="1954 Geneva Conference">Geneva Conference of 1954</a>. In 1960, amidst a series of rebellions in the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Laos" title="Kingdom of Laos">Kingdom of Laos</a>, fighting broke out between the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Lao_Army" title="Royal Lao Army">Royal Lao Army</a> (RLA) and the communist <a href="/wiki/North_Vietnam" title="North Vietnam">North Vietnamese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>-backed Pathet Lao guerillas. A second Provisional Government of National Unity formed by Prince <a href="/wiki/Souvanna_Phouma" title="Souvanna Phouma">Souvanna Phouma</a> in 1962 was unsuccessful, and the situation steadily deteriorated into large scale <a href="/wiki/Laotian_Civil_War" title="Laotian Civil War">civil war</a> between the Royal Laotian government and the Pathet Lao. The Pathet Lao were backed militarily by the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Army_of_Vietnam" title="People's Army of Vietnam">People's Army of Vietnam</a> (PAVN) and the <a href="/wiki/Viet_Cong" title="Viet Cong">Viet Cong</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-britannica_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-45">[45]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Muang_Khoun_-_Laos_-_01.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Muang_Khoun_-_Laos_-_01.JPG/220px-Muang_Khoun_-_Laos_-_01.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Muang_Khoun_-_Laos_-_01.JPG/330px-Muang_Khoun_-_Laos_-_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Muang_Khoun_-_Laos_-_01.JPG/440px-Muang_Khoun_-_Laos_-_01.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Muang_Khoun_-_Laos_-_01.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ruins of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Muang_Khoun&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Muang Khoun (page does not exist)">Muang Khoun</a>, former capital of <a href="/wiki/Xiangkhouang_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Xiangkhouang Province">Xiangkhouang province</a>, destroyed by the <a href="/wiki/CIA_activities_in_Laos" title="CIA activities in Laos">American bombing of Laos</a> in the late 1960s
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Laos was a key part of the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> since parts of Laos were invaded and occupied by <a href="/wiki/North_Vietnam" title="North Vietnam">North Vietnam</a> for use as a supply route for its war against <a href="/wiki/South_Vietnam" title="South Vietnam">South Vietnam</a>. In response, the United States initiated a bombing campaign against the PAVN positions, supported regular and irregular anticommunist forces in Laos, and supported <a href="/wiki/Army_of_the_Republic_of_Vietnam" title="Army of the Republic of Vietnam">Army of the Republic of Vietnam</a> <a href="/wiki/CIA_activities_in_Laos" title="CIA activities in Laos">incursions into Laos</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_46-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-britannica_45-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-45">[45]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1968, the PAVN launched a multi-division attack to help the Pathet Lao fight the RLA. The attack resulted in the RLA largely demobilising, leaving the conflict to irregular ethnic <a href="/wiki/Hmong_people" title="Hmong people">Hmong</a> forces of the "Secret Army" backed by the United States and Thailand, and led by General <a href="/wiki/Vang_Pao" title="Vang Pao">Vang Pao</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Massive aerial bombardments against the PAVN/Pathet Lao forces were carried out by the United States to prevent the collapse of the Kingdom of Laos central government, and to deny the use of the <a href="/wiki/Ho_Chi_Minh_trail" title="Ho Chi Minh trail">Ho Chi Minh Trail</a> to attack US forces in South Vietnam.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_46-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-46">[46]</a></sup> Between 1964 and 1973, the US dropped two million tons of bombs on Laos, nearly equal to the 2.1&nbsp;million tons of bombs the US dropped on Europe and Asia during all of World War II, making Laos the most heavily bombed country in history relative to the size of its population; <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> notes this was "nearly a ton for every person in Laos".<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Some 80&nbsp;million bombs failed to explode and remain scattered throughout the country, rendering vast swaths of land impossible to cultivate and killing or maiming approximately 50 Laotians every year.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Because of the particularly heavy impact of <a href="/wiki/Cluster_munition" title="Cluster munition">cluster bombs</a> during this war, Laos was a strong advocate of the <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_Cluster_Munitions" title="Convention on Cluster Munitions">Convention on Cluster Munitions</a> to ban the weapons and was host to the First Meeting of States Parties to the convention in November 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vientianne1973.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Vientianne1973.jpg/220px-Vientianne1973.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Vientianne1973.jpg/330px-Vientianne1973.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Vientianne1973.jpg/440px-Vientianne1973.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2260" data-file-height="1822"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vientianne1973.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Pathet_Lao" title="Pathet Lao">Pathet Lao</a> soldiers in <a href="/wiki/Vientiane" title="Vientiane">Vientiane</a>, 1972
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1975 the Pathet Lao overthrew the royalist government, forcing King <a href="/wiki/Sisavang_Vatthana" title="Sisavang Vatthana">Savang Vatthana</a> to abdicate on 2 December 1975. He later died under suspicious circumstances in a <a href="/wiki/Re-education_camp_(Vietnam)" title="Re-education camp (Vietnam)">re-education camp</a>. Between 20,000 and 62,000 Laotians died during the civil war.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_46-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> The royalists set up a <a href="/wiki/Royal_Lao_Government_in_Exile" title="Royal Lao Government in Exile">government in exile</a> in the United States. </p>
      <p>On 2 December 1975, after taking control of the country, the Pathet Lao government under <a href="/wiki/Kaysone_Phomvihane" title="Kaysone Phomvihane">Kaysone Phomvihane</a> renamed the country as the <i>Lao People's Democratic Republic</i> and signed agreements giving Vietnam the right to station armed forces and to appoint advisers to assist in overseeing the country. The close ties between Laos and Vietnam were formalised via a treaty signed in 1977, which has since provided direction for Lao foreign policy, and provides the basis for Vietnamese involvement at all levels of Lao political and economic life.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_46-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Martin_Stuart-Fox_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Martin_Stuart-Fox-51">[51]</a></sup> Laos was requested in 1979 by Vietnam to end relations with the People's Republic of China, leading to isolation in trade by China, the United States, and other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-DamienKingsbury_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DamienKingsbury-52">[52]</a></sup> In 1979, there were 50,000 PAVN troops stationed in Laos and as many as 6,000 civilian Vietnamese officials including 1,000 directly attached to the ministries in Vientiane.<sup id="cite_ref-Savada_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Savada-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Prayaga_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Prayaga-54">[54]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The conflict between Hmong rebels and Laos <a href="/wiki/Insurgency_in_Laos" title="Insurgency in Laos">continued in key areas</a> of Laos, including in Saysaboune Closed Military Zone, Xaisamboune Closed Military Zone near Vientiane Province and <a href="/wiki/Xiangkhouang_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Xiangkhouang Province">Xiangkhouang Province</a>. From 1975 to 1996, the United States resettled some <a href="/wiki/Indochina_refugee_crisis" title="Indochina refugee crisis">250,000 Lao refugees</a> from Thailand, including 130,000 Hmong.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Laos" title="Geography of Laos">Geography of Laos</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mekong_River_(Luang_Prabang).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Mekong_River_%28Luang_Prabang%29.jpg/220px-Mekong_River_%28Luang_Prabang%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="101" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Mekong_River_%28Luang_Prabang%29.jpg/330px-Mekong_River_%28Luang_Prabang%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Mekong_River_%28Luang_Prabang%29.jpg/440px-Mekong_River_%28Luang_Prabang%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4592" data-file-height="2100"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mekong_River_(Luang_Prabang).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Mekong_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Mekong River">Mekong River</a> flowing through <a href="/wiki/Luang_Prabang" title="Luang Prabang">Luang Prabang</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Laos_ricefields.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Laos_ricefields.JPG/220px-Laos_ricefields.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Laos_ricefields.JPG/330px-Laos_ricefields.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Laos_ricefields.JPG/440px-Laos_ricefields.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Laos_ricefields.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Paddy_fields" class="mw-redirect" title="Paddy fields">Paddy fields</a> in Laos
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Laos is the only landlocked country in Southeast Asia, and it lies mostly between latitudes <a href="/wiki/14th_parallel_north" title="14th parallel north">14°</a> and <a href="/wiki/23rd_parallel_north" title="23rd parallel north">23°N</a> (a small area is south of 14°), and longitudes <a href="/wiki/100th_meridian_east" title="100th meridian east">100°</a> and <a href="/wiki/108th_meridian_east" title="108th meridian east">108°E</a>. Its thickly forested landscape consists mostly of rugged mountains, the highest of which is <a href="/wiki/Phou_Bia" title="Phou Bia">Phou Bia</a> at 2,818 metres (9,245&nbsp;ft), with some plains and plateaus. The Mekong River forms a large part of the western boundary with Thailand, where the mountains of the <a href="/wiki/Annamite_Range" title="Annamite Range">Annamite Range</a> form most of the eastern border with Vietnam and the <a href="/wiki/Luang_Prabang_Range" title="Luang Prabang Range">Luang Prabang Range</a> the northwestern border with the <a href="/wiki/Thai_highlands" title="Thai highlands">Thai highlands</a>. There are two plateaux, the <a href="/wiki/Xiangkhoang_Plateau" title="Xiangkhoang Plateau">Xiangkhoang</a> in the north and the <a href="/wiki/Bolaven_Plateau" title="Bolaven Plateau">Bolaven Plateau</a> at the southern end. Laos can be considered to consist of three geographical areas: north, central, and south.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-56">[56]</a></sup> Laos had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 5.59/10, ranking it 98<sup>th</sup> globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-57">[57]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1993 the Laos government set aside 21% of the nation's land area for habitat conservation preservation.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> The country is one of four in the opium poppy growing region known as the "<a href="/wiki/Golden_Triangle_(Southeast_Asia)" title="Golden Triangle (Southeast Asia)">Golden Triangle</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> According to the October 2007 UNODC fact book <i>Opium Poppy Cultivation in South East Asia</i>, the poppy cultivation area was 15 square kilometres (5.8&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), down from 18 square kilometres (6.9&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_LAO_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Koppen-Geiger_Map_LAO_present.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_LAO_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Koppen-Geiger_Map_LAO_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_LAO_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Koppen-Geiger_Map_LAO_present.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_LAO_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1290" data-file-height="850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_LAO_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Laos map of Köppen climate classification.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The climate is mostly tropical savanna and influenced by the <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a> pattern.<sup id="cite_ref-climate_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-climate-61">[61]</a></sup> There is a distinct rainy season from May to October, followed by a dry season from November to April. Local tradition holds that there are three seasons (rainy, cool and hot) as the latter two months of the climatologically defined dry season are noticeably hotter than the earlier four months.<sup id="cite_ref-climate_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-climate-61">[61]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Laos" title="Administrative divisions of Laos">Administrative divisions of Laos</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Laos is divided into 17 <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Laos" title="Provinces of Laos">provinces</a> (<i>khoueng</i>) and one prefecture (<i>kampheng nakhon</i>), which includes the capital city Vientiane (<i>Nakhon Louang Viangchan</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> A new province, <a href="/wiki/Xaisomboun_Province" title="Xaisomboun Province">Xaisomboun Province</a>, was established on 13 December 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Provinces are further divided into <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Laos" title="Districts of Laos">districts</a> (<i>muang</i>) and then villages (<i>ban</i>). An "urban" village is essentially a town.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-56">[56]</a></sup> </p>
