      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Laos" title="Politics of Laos">Politics of Laos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Laos" title="Foreign relations of Laos">Foreign relations of Laos</a>
      </div> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:271px;max-width:271px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:139px;max-width:139px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Thongloun_Sisoulith_with_Obamas_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Thongloun_Sisoulith_with_Obamas_cropped.jpg/137px-Thongloun_Sisoulith_with_Obamas_cropped.jpg" decoding="async" width="137" height="183" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Thongloun_Sisoulith_with_Obamas_cropped.jpg/206px-Thongloun_Sisoulith_with_Obamas_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Thongloun_Sisoulith_with_Obamas_cropped.jpg/274px-Thongloun_Sisoulith_with_Obamas_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="400"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">
           <a href="/wiki/Thongloun_Sisoulith" title="Thongloun Sisoulith">Thongloun Sisoulith</a>
           <br><small>General Secretary and Prime Minister</small>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:128px;max-width:128px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Bounnhang_Vorachith_2016_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Bounnhang_Vorachith_2016_%28cropped%29.jpg/126px-Bounnhang_Vorachith_2016_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="126" height="182" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Bounnhang_Vorachith_2016_%28cropped%29.jpg/189px-Bounnhang_Vorachith_2016_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Bounnhang_Vorachith_2016_%28cropped%29.jpg/252px-Bounnhang_Vorachith_2016_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="361" data-file-height="522"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">
           <a href="/wiki/Bounnhang_Vorachith" title="Bounnhang Vorachith">Bounnhang Vorachith</a>
           <br><small>President</small>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Lao People's Democratic Republic is one of the world's only <a href="/wiki/Socialist_state" title="Socialist state">socialist states</a> openly endorsing <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">communism</a>. The only legal political party is the <a href="/wiki/Lao_People%27s_Revolutionary_Party" title="Lao People's Revolutionary Party">Lao People's Revolutionary Party</a> (LPRP). With <a href="/wiki/One-party_state" title="One-party state">one-party state</a> status of Laos, the <a href="/wiki/General_Secretary_of_the_Lao_People%27s_Revolutionary_Party" title="General Secretary of the Lao People's Revolutionary Party">General Secretary</a> (<a href="/wiki/Party_leader" title="Party leader">party leader</a>) holds ultimate power and authority over state and government and serves as the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_leader" title="Supreme leader">supreme leader</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_46-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-46">[46]</a></sup> The head of state is <a href="/wiki/President_of_Laos" title="President of Laos">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Bounnhang_Vorachith" title="Bounnhang Vorachith">Bounnhang Vorachith</a>. The <a href="/wiki/General_Secretary_of_the_Lao_People%27s_Revolutionary_Party" title="General Secretary of the Lao People's Revolutionary Party">General Secretary of the Lao People's Revolutionary Party</a> is <a href="/wiki/Thongloun_Sisoulith" title="Thongloun Sisoulith">Thongloun Sisoulith</a>, who is serving as the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_leader" title="Supreme leader">supreme leader</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The head of government is Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Thongloun_Sisoulith" title="Thongloun Sisoulith">Thongloun Sisoulith</a>, who is also the head of the Lao People's Revolutionary <a href="/wiki/Politburo_of_the_Lao_People%27s_Revolutionary_Party" title="Politburo of the Lao People's Revolutionary Party">Party's Politburo</a>. Government policies are determined by the party through the all-powerful eleven-member <a href="/wiki/Politburo_of_the_Lao_People%27s_Revolutionary_Party" title="Politburo of the Lao People's Revolutionary Party">Politburo of the Lao People's Revolutionary Party</a> and the 61-member <a href="/wiki/Central_Committee_of_the_Lao_People%27s_Revolutionary_Party" title="Central Committee of the Lao People's Revolutionary Party">Central Committee of the Lao People's Revolutionary Party</a>. </p>
      <p>Laos's first French-written and monarchical constitution was promulgated on 11 May 1947, and declared Laos an independent state within the <a href="/wiki/French_Union" title="French Union">French Union</a>. The revised constitution of 11 May 1957 omitted reference to the French Union, though close educational, health and technical ties with the former colonial power persisted. The 1957 document was abrogated in December 1975, when a communist people's republic was proclaimed. A new constitution was adopted in 1991 and enshrined a "leading role" for the LPRP.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_46-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-46">[46]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Lao_People%27s_Revolutionary_Party.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Flag_of_the_Lao_People%27s_Revolutionary_Party.svg/200px-Flag_of_the_Lao_People%27s_Revolutionary_Party.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Flag_of_the_Lao_People%27s_Revolutionary_Party.svg/300px-Flag_of_the_Lao_People%27s_Revolutionary_Party.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Flag_of_the_Lao_People%27s_Revolutionary_Party.svg/400px-Flag_of_the_Lao_People%27s_Revolutionary_Party.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Lao_People%27s_Revolutionary_Party.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Flag of the ruling <a href="/wiki/Lao_People%27s_Revolutionary_Party" title="Lao People's Revolutionary Party">Lao People's Revolutionary Party</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The National Assembly, which essentially acts as a <a href="/wiki/Rubber_stamp_(politics)" title="Rubber stamp (politics)">rubber stamp</a> for the LPRP, approves all new laws, although the executive branch retains authority to issue binding decrees. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_and_ASEAN_heads_of_state_and_government_at_the_Rashtrapati_Bhavan_in_New_Delhi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_and_ASEAN_heads_of_state_and_government_at_the_Rashtrapati_Bhavan_in_New_Delhi.jpg/220px-Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_and_ASEAN_heads_of_state_and_government_at_the_Rashtrapati_Bhavan_in_New_Delhi.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_and_ASEAN_heads_of_state_and_government_at_the_Rashtrapati_Bhavan_in_New_Delhi.jpg/330px-Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_and_ASEAN_heads_of_state_and_government_at_the_Rashtrapati_Bhavan_in_New_Delhi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_and_ASEAN_heads_of_state_and_government_at_the_Rashtrapati_Bhavan_in_New_Delhi.jpg/440px-Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_and_ASEAN_heads_of_state_and_government_at_the_Rashtrapati_Bhavan_in_New_Delhi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1350" data-file-height="900"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_and_ASEAN_heads_of_state_and_government_at_the_Rashtrapati_Bhavan_in_New_Delhi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Thongloun_Sisoulith" title="Thongloun Sisoulith">Thongloun Sisoulith</a> with Indian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Narendra_Modi" title="Narendra Modi">Narendra Modi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations" class="mw-redirect" title="Association of Southeast Asian Nations">ASEAN</a> heads of state in New Delhi on 25 January 2018
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The foreign relations of Laos after the takeover by the Pathet Lao in December 1975 were characterised by a hostile posture toward the West, with the government of the Lao People's Democratic Republic aligning itself with the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Bloc" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet Bloc">Soviet Bloc</a>, maintaining close ties with the Soviet Union and depending heavily on the Soviets for most of its foreign assistance.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Laos also maintained a "special relationship" with Vietnam and formalised a 1977 treaty of friendship and cooperation that created tensions with China.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%A1_%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BC%D1%8C%D0%B5%D1%80-%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%9B%D0%B0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%BE-%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%A0%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BF%D1%83%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%A2%D1%85%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B3%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%83%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BC.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/%D0%A1_%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BC%D1%8C%D0%B5%D1%80-%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%9B%D0%B0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%BE-%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%A0%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BF%D1%83%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%A2%D1%85%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B3%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%83%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BC.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/%D0%A1_%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BC%D1%8C%D0%B5%D1%80-%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%9B%D0%B0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%BE-%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%A0%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BF%D1%83%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%A2%D1%85%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B3%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%83%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BC.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/%D0%A1_%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BC%D1%8C%D0%B5%D1%80-%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%9B%D0%B0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%BE-%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%A0%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BF%D1%83%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%A2%D1%85%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B3%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%83%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BC.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1880" data-file-height="1160"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%A1_%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BC%D1%8C%D0%B5%D1%80-%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%9B%D0%B0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%BE-%D0%94%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%A0%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BF%D1%83%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%A2%D1%85%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B3%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%83%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BC.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Thongloun_Sisoulith" title="Thongloun Sisoulith">Thongloun Sisoulith</a> with Russian President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> in 2016
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Laos's emergence from <a href="/wiki/International_isolation" title="International isolation">international isolation</a> has been marked through improved and expanded relations with other nations such as <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Laos%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="Laos–United States relations">Trade relations with the United States</a> were normalised in November 2004 through Congress approved legislation.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Laos was admitted into the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations" class="mw-redirect" title="Association of Southeast Asian Nations">Association of Southeast Asian Nations</a> (ASEAN) in July 1997 and acceded to the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> In 2005 it attended the inaugural <a href="/wiki/East_Asia_Summit" title="East Asia Summit">East Asia Summit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lao_People%27s_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Lao People's Army">Lao People's Army</a>
      </div> 
      <p>On 17 May 2014, Defense Minister and Deputy Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Douangchay_Phichit" title="Douangchay Phichit">Douangchay Phichit</a> was killed in a plane crash, along with other top ranking officials.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> The officials were to participate in a ceremony to mark the liberation of the Plain of Jars from the former Royal Lao government forces.<sup id="cite_ref-theg_Laos_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theg_Laos-71">[71]</a></sup> Their Russian-built <a href="/wiki/Antonov_An-74" title="Antonov An-74">Antonov AN 74-300</a> with 20 people on board crashed in <a href="/wiki/Xiangkhouang" title="Xiangkhouang">Xiangkhouang</a> Province.<sup id="cite_ref-PlaneCrash_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PlaneCrash-72">[72]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hmong_conflict">Hmong conflict</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Hmong conflict">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Some Hmong groups fought as CIA-backed units on the royalist side in the <a href="/wiki/Laotian_Civil_War" title="Laotian Civil War">Laotian Civil War</a>. After the Pathet Lao took over the country in 1975, the conflict continued in isolated pockets. In 1977, a communist newspaper promised the party would hunt down the "American collaborators" and their families "to the last root".<sup id="cite_ref-timesonline2006_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timesonline2006-73">[73]</a></sup> As many as 200,000 Hmong went into exile in Thailand, with many ending up in the US. Other Hmong fighters hid out in mountains in Xiangkhouang Province for many years, with a remnant emerging from the jungle in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-timesonline2006_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timesonline2006-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1989, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Refugees" title="United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees">United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees</a> (UNHCR), with the support of the US government, instituted the <a href="/wiki/Comprehensive_Plan_of_Action" title="Comprehensive Plan of Action">Comprehensive Plan of Action</a>, a programme to stem the tide of <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_boat_people" title="Vietnamese boat people">Indochinese refugees</a> from Laos, Vietnam, and Cambodia. Under the plan, refugee status was evaluated through a screening process. Recognised asylum seekers were given resettlement opportunities, while the remaining refugees were to be repatriated under guarantee of safety. After talks with the UNHCR and the Thai government, Laos agreed to repatriate the 60,000 Lao refugees living in Thailand, including several thousand Hmong people. Very few of the Lao refugees, however, were willing to return voluntarily.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Pressure to resettle the refugees grew as the Thai government worked to close its remaining refugee camps. While some Hmong people returned to Laos voluntarily, with development assistance from UNHCR, allegations of forced repatriation surfaced.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Of those Hmong who did return to Laos, some quickly escaped back to Thailand, describing discrimination and brutal treatment at the hands of Lao authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hmong_girls_in_Laos_1973_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Hmong_girls_in_Laos_1973_2.jpg/170px-Hmong_girls_in_Laos_1973_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="230" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Hmong_girls_in_Laos_1973_2.jpg/255px-Hmong_girls_in_Laos_1973_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Hmong_girls_in_Laos_1973_2.jpg/340px-Hmong_girls_in_Laos_1973_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="523" data-file-height="707"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Hmong_girls_in_Laos_1973_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Hmong girls in Laos, 1973
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1993, Vue Mai, a former Hmong soldier and leader of the largest Hmong refugee camp in Thailand, who had been recruited by the US&nbsp;Embassy in <a href="/wiki/Bangkok" title="Bangkok">Bangkok</a> to return to Laos as proof of the repatriation programme's success, disappeared in Vientiane. According to the US&nbsp;Committee for Refugees, he was arrested by Lao security forces and was never seen again.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Following the Vue Mai incident, debate over the Hmong's planned repatriation to Laos intensified greatly, especially in the United States, where it drew strong opposition from many <a href="/wiki/Conservatism_in_the_United_States" title="Conservatism in the United States">American conservatives</a> and some human rights advocates. In a 23 October 1995 <i><a href="/wiki/National_Review" title="National Review">National Review</a></i> article, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Johns_(policy_analyst)" title="Michael Johns (policy analyst)">Michael Johns</a>, the former <a href="/wiki/The_Heritage_Foundation" title="The Heritage Foundation">Heritage Foundation</a> foreign policy expert and <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a> <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> aide, labelled the Hmong's repatriation a <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Bill_Clinton" title="Presidency of Bill Clinton">Clinton administration</a> "betrayal", describing the Hmong as a people "who have spilled their blood in defense of American geopolitical interests".<sup id="cite_ref-web.archive.org_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web.archive.org-78">[78]</a></sup> Debate on the issue escalated quickly. In an effort to halt the planned repatriation, the Republican-led <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">US&nbsp;Senate</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">House of Representatives</a> both appropriated funds for the remaining Thailand-based Hmong to be immediately resettled in the United States; Clinton, however, responded by promising a veto of the legislation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In their opposition of the repatriation plans, Democratic and Republican Members of Congress challenged the Clinton administration's position that the government of Laos was not systematically violating Hmong human rights. US Representative <a href="/wiki/Steve_Gunderson" title="Steve Gunderson">Steve Gunderson</a>, for instance, told a Hmong gathering: "I do not enjoy standing up and saying to my government that you are not telling the truth, but if that is necessary to defend truth and justice, I will do that."<sup id="cite_ref-web.archive.org_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web.archive.org-78">[78]</a></sup> Republicans called several Congressional hearings on alleged persecution of the Hmong in Laos in an apparent attempt to generate further support for their opposition to the Hmong's repatriation to Laos. </p>
      <p>Although some accusations of forced repatriation were denied,<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> thousands of Hmong people refused to return to Laos. In 1996 as the deadline for the closure of Thai refugee camps approached, and under mounting political pressure, the United States agreed to resettle Hmong refugees who passed a new screening process.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Around 5,000 Hmong people who were not resettled at the time of the camp closures sought asylum at <a href="/wiki/Wat_Tham_Krabok" title="Wat Tham Krabok">Wat Tham Krabok</a>, a Buddhist monastery in central Thailand where more than 10,000 Hmong refugees had already been living. The Thai government attempted to repatriate these refugees, but the Wat Tham Krabok Hmong refused to leave and the Lao government refused to accept them, claiming they were involved in the <a href="/wiki/Illegal_drug_trade" title="Illegal drug trade">illegal drug trade</a> and were of non-Lao origin.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Following threats of forcible removal by the Thai government, the United States, in a significant victory for the Hmong, agreed to accept 15,000 of the refugees in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Several thousand Hmong people, fearing forced repatriation to Laos if they were not accepted for resettlement in the United States, fled the camp to live elsewhere within Thailand where a sizeable Hmong population has been present since the 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> In 2004 and 2005, thousands of Hmong fled from the jungles of Laos to a temporary refugee camp in the Thai province of <a href="/wiki/Phetchabun_Province" title="Phetchabun Province">Phetchabun</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Lending further support to earlier claims that the government of Laos was persecuting the Hmong, filmmaker Rebecca Sommer documented first-hand accounts in her documentary, <i>Hunted Like Animals</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> and in a comprehensive report that includes summaries of refugee claims and was submitted to the UN in May 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-EU@UN_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EU@UN-87">[87]</a></sup> UNHCHR, and international groups have since spoken out about the forced repatriation.<sup id="cite_ref-EU@UN_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EU@UN-87">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> The Thai foreign ministry has said that it will halt deportation of Hmong refugees held in Detention Centres in <a href="/wiki/Nong_Khai" title="Nong Khai">Nong Khai</a>, while talks are underway to resettle them in Australia, Canada, the Netherlands and the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> Plans to resettle additional Hmong refugees in the United States were stalled by provisions of President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush's</a> <a href="/wiki/Patriot_Act" title="Patriot Act">Patriot Act</a> and <a href="/wiki/Real_ID_Act" title="Real ID Act">Real ID Act</a>, under which Hmong veterans of the Secret War, who fought on the side of the United States, are classified as terrorists because of their historical involvement in armed conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Laos" title="Human rights in Laos">Human rights in Laos</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Human rights violations remain a significant concern in Laos.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-94">[94]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">Democracy Index</a> 2016</i> Laos was classified as an "authoritarian regime", ranking lowest of the nine <a href="/wiki/ASEAN" title="ASEAN">ASEAN</a> nations included in the study.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Prominent civil society advocates, human rights defenders, political and religious dissidents, and Hmong refugees have disappeared at the hands of Lao military and security forces.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ostensibly, the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Laos" title="Constitution of Laos">Constitution of Laos</a> that was promulgated in 1991 and amended in 2003 contains most key safeguards for human rights. For example, Article 8 makes it clear that Laos is a <a href="/wiki/Multinational_state" title="Multinational state">multinational state</a> and is committed to equality between ethnic groups. The constitution also contains provisions for <a href="/wiki/Gender_equality" title="Gender equality">gender equality</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">freedom of religion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">freedom of speech</a>, and freedom of press and assembly.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> On 25 September 2009, Laos ratified the <a href="/wiki/International_Covenant_on_Civil_and_Political_Rights" title="International Covenant on Civil and Political Rights">International Covenant on Civil and Political Rights</a>, nine years after signing the treaty. The stated policy objectives of both the Lao government and international donors remain focused upon achieving sustainable economic growth and poverty reduction.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>However, the government of Laos frequently breaches its own constitution and the rule of law, since the judiciary and judges are appointed by the ruling communist party. According to independent non-profit/non-governmental organizations (NGOs) such as <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Amnesty_International_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amnesty_International-101">[101]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> and Civil Rights Defenders,<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> along with the US State Department,<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> serious human rights violations such as arbitrary detentions, disappearances, free speech restrictions, prison abuses and other violations are an ongoing problem. Amnesty International raised concerns about the ratification record of the Lao government on human rights standards and its lack of co-operation with the UN human rights mechanisms and legislative measures—both impact negatively upon human rights.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-94">[94]</a></sup> The organisation also raised concerns in relation to freedom of expression, poor prison conditions, restrictions on freedom of religions, protection of refugees and asylum-seekers, and the death penalty.<sup id="cite_ref-Amnesty_International_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amnesty_International-101">[101]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In October 1999, 30 young people were arrested for attempting to display posters calling for peaceful economic, political and social change in Laos. Five of them were arrested and subsequently sentenced to up to 10 years imprisonment on charges of treason. They were to have been released by October 2009, but their whereabouts remain unknown.<sup id="cite_ref-Amnesty_International_101-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amnesty_International-101">[101]</a></sup> Later reports have contradicted this, claiming they were sentenced to 20 years in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-Worldwide_Movement_for_Human_Rights_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Worldwide_Movement_for_Human_Rights-105">[105]</a></sup> In late February 2017, two of those imprisoned were finally released after 17 years.<sup id="cite_ref-Sombath.org_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sombath.org-106">[106]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Laos and Vietnamese (SRV) troops were reported to have raped and killed four Christian Hmong women in Xiangkhouang Province in 2011, according to the US-based non-governmental public policy research organization <a href="/wiki/The_Centre_for_Public_Policy_Analysis" class="mw-redirect" title="The Centre for Public Policy Analysis">The Centre for Public Policy Analysis</a>, which also said other Christian and independent Buddhist and <a href="/wiki/Tai_folk_religion" title="Tai folk religion">animist</a> believers were being persecuted.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Human rights advocates including <a href="/wiki/Vang_Pobzeb" title="Vang Pobzeb">Vang Pobzeb</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kerry_and_Kay_Danes" title="Kerry and Kay Danes">Kerry and Kay Danes</a>, and others have also raised concerns about human rights violations, torture, the arrest and detention of political prisoners as well as the detention of foreign prisoners in Laos including at the infamous <a href="/wiki/Phonthong_Prison" title="Phonthong Prison">Phonthong Prison</a> in Vientiane.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>According to estimates, around 300,000 people fled to Thailand as a consequence of governmental repressions. Amongst them, 100,000 Hmongs—30% of the entire Hmong population—and 90% of all of Lao intellectuals, specialists, and officials. Moreover, 130,000 deaths can be attributed to the civil war.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> Laos is an origin country for sexually trafficked persons.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> A number of citizens, primarily women and girls from all <a href="/wiki/List_of_ethnic_groups_in_Laos" title="List of ethnic groups in Laos">ethnic groups</a> and foreigners, have been victims of <a href="/wiki/Sex_trafficking_in_Laos" title="Sex trafficking in Laos">sex trafficking in Laos</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Laos" title="Economy of Laos">Economy of Laos</a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rice_planting_near_Champasak_(Laos).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Rice_planting_near_Champasak_%28Laos%29.jpg/220px-Rice_planting_near_Champasak_%28Laos%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Rice_planting_near_Champasak_%28Laos%29.jpg/330px-Rice_planting_near_Champasak_%28Laos%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Rice_planting_near_Champasak_%28Laos%29.jpg/440px-Rice_planting_near_Champasak_%28Laos%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rice_planting_near_Champasak_(Laos).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>About 80% of the Laotian population practises <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_agriculture" title="Subsistence agriculture">subsistence agriculture</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>The Lao economy depends on investment and trade with its neighbors, Thailand, Vietnam, and, especially in the north, China. <a href="/wiki/Pakse" title="Pakse">Pakxe</a> has also experienced growth based on cross-border trade with Thailand and Vietnam. In 2009, despite the fact that the government is still officially communist, the Obama administration in the US declared Laos was no longer a Marxist-Leninist state and lifted bans on Laotian companies receiving financing from the <a href="/wiki/Export%E2%80%93Import_Bank_of_the_United_States" title="Export–Import Bank of the United States">US Export-Import Bank</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2016, China was the biggest foreign investor in Laos's economy, having invested in US$5.395&nbsp;billion since 1989, according to Laos Ministry of Planning and Investment's 1989–2014 report. Thailand (invested US$4.489&nbsp;billion) and Vietnam (invested US$3.108&nbsp;billion) are the second and third largest investors respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> The economy receives <a href="/wiki/Development_aid" title="Development aid">development aid</a> from the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a>, and other international sources; and also <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a> for development of the society, industry, <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">hydropower</a> and mining (most notably of copper and gold). </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Subsistence_agriculture" title="Subsistence agriculture">Subsistence agriculture</a> still accounts for half of the GDP and provides 80% of employment. Only 4% of the country is arable land and a mere 0.3% used as permanent crop land,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> the lowest percentage in the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Mekong_Subregion" title="Greater Mekong Subregion">Greater Mekong Subregion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> The irrigated areas under cultivation account for only 28% of the total area under cultivation which, in turn, represents only 12% of all of the agricultural land in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> Rice dominates agriculture, with about 80% of the arable land area used for growing rice.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> Approximately 77% of Lao farm households are self-sufficient in rice.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Laos may have the greatest number of rice varieties in the Greater Mekong Subregion. The Lao government has been working with the <a href="/wiki/International_Rice_Research_Institute" title="International Rice Research Institute">International Rice Research Institute</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> to collect seed samples of each of the thousands of rice varieties found in Laos.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Morning_market_in_Vientiane.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Morning_market_in_Vientiane.JPG/220px-Morning_market_in_Vientiane.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Morning_market_in_Vientiane.JPG/330px-Morning_market_in_Vientiane.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Morning_market_in_Vientiane.JPG/440px-Morning_market_in_Vientiane.JPG 2x" data-file-width="474" data-file-height="315"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Morning_market_in_Vientiane.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Morning market in Vientiane
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Laos is rich in mineral resources and imports petroleum and gas. Metallurgy is an important industry, and the government hopes to attract foreign investment to develop the substantial deposits of coal, gold, bauxite, tin, copper, and other valuable metals. The <a href="/wiki/Mining_industry_of_Laos" title="Mining industry of Laos">mining industry of Laos</a> has received prominent attention with foreign direct investments. This sector has made significant contributions to the economic condition of Laos. More than 540 mineral deposits of gold, copper, zinc, lead and other minerals have been identified, explored and mined.<sup id="cite_ref-Kyophilvong_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kyophilvong-123">[123]</a></sup> In addition, the country's plentiful water resources and mountainous terrain enable it to produce and export large quantities of hydroelectric energy. Of the potential capacity of approximately 18,000 megawatts, around 8,000 megawatts have been committed for export to Thailand and Vietnam.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2018, the country <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">ranked 139th</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> (HDI), indicating medium development.<sup id="cite_ref-UNDP_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNDP-125">[125]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Global_Hunger_Index" title="Global Hunger Index">Global Hunger Index</a> (2018), Laos ranks as the 36th hungriest nation in the world out of the list of the 52 nations with the worst hunger situation(s).<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> In 2019, the UN Special Rapporteur on extreme poverty and human rights conducted an official visit to Laos and found that the country's top-down approach to economic growth and poverty alleviation "is all too often counterproductive, leading to impoverishment and jeopardizing the rights of the poor and marginalised."<sup id="cite_ref-OHCHR_March_2019_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OHCHR_March_2019-127">[127]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country's most widely recognised product may well be <a href="/wiki/Beerlao" title="Beerlao">Beerlao</a>, which in 2017 was exported to more than 20 countries worldwide. It is produced by the <a href="/wiki/Lao_Brewery_Company" title="Lao Brewery Company">Lao Brewery Company</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Laos" title="Tourism in Laos">Tourism in Laos</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:ViewFromWatPhu.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/ViewFromWatPhu.JPG/220px-ViewFromWatPhu.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/ViewFromWatPhu.JPG/330px-ViewFromWatPhu.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/ViewFromWatPhu.JPG/440px-ViewFromWatPhu.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:ViewFromWatPhu.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Near the sanctuary on the main upper level of <a href="/wiki/Vat_Phou" title="Vat Phou">Vat Phou</a>, looking back towards the <a href="/wiki/Mekong_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Mekong River">Mekong River</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The tourism sector has grown rapidly, from 80,000 international visitors in 1990, to 1.876&nbsp;million in 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> when tourism had been expected to rise to US$1.5857&nbsp;billion by 2020. In 2010, one in every 11 jobs was in the tourism sector. Export earnings from international visitors and tourism goods are expected to generate 16% of total exports or US$270.3&nbsp;million in 2010, growing in nominal terms to US$484.2&nbsp;million (12.5% of the total) in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> The European Council on Trade and Tourism awarded the country the "World Best Tourist Destination" designation for 2013 for architecture and history.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Luang_Prabang" title="Luang Prabang">Luang Prabang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vat_Phou" title="Vat Phou">Vat Phou</a> are both <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage">UNESCO World Heritage</a> sites. Major festivals include Lao New Year celebrated around 13–15 April and involves a <a href="/wiki/Water_festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Water festival">water festival</a> similar but more subdued than that of Thailand and other Southeast Asian countries. </p>
      <p>The Lao National Tourism Administration, related government agencies and the private sector are working together to realise the vision put forth in the country's National Ecotourism Strategy and Action Plan. This includes decreasing the environmental and cultural impact of tourism; increasing awareness in the importance of ethnic groups and biological diversity; providing a source of income to conserve, sustain and manage the Lao protected area network and cultural heritage sites; and emphasizing the need for tourism zoning and management plans for sites that will be developed as <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism" title="Ecotourism">ecotourism</a> destinations.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Laos" title="Transport in Laos">Transport in Laos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Laos" class="mw-redirect" title="Telecommunications in Laos">Telecommunications in Laos</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nam_ou_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Nam_ou_1.jpg/220px-Nam_ou_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Nam_ou_1.jpg/330px-Nam_ou_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Nam_ou_1.jpg/440px-Nam_ou_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1568" data-file-height="1160"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nam_ou_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Rivers are an important means of transport in Laos.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The main international airports are Vientiane's <a href="/wiki/Wattay_International_Airport" title="Wattay International Airport">Wattay International Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luang_Prabang_International_Airport" title="Luang Prabang International Airport">Luang Prabang International Airport</a> with <a href="/wiki/Pakse_International_Airport" title="Pakse International Airport">Pakse International Airport</a> also having a few international flights. The national carrier is <a href="/wiki/Lao_Airlines" title="Lao Airlines">Lao Airlines</a>. Other carriers serving the country include <a href="/wiki/Bangkok_Airways" title="Bangkok Airways">Bangkok Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_Airlines" title="Vietnam Airlines">Vietnam Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/AirAsia" title="AirAsia">AirAsia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thai_Airways" title="Thai Airways">Thai Airways</a> and <a href="/wiki/China_Eastern_Airlines" title="China Eastern Airlines">China Eastern Airlines</a>. </p>
      <p>Much of Laos lacks adequate infrastructure. Laos' railways include a short link to connect Vientiane with Thailand over the <a href="/wiki/First_Thai%E2%80%93Lao_Friendship_Bridge" title="First Thai–Lao Friendship Bridge">Thai–Lao Friendship Bridge</a>, and a short <a href="/wiki/Portage_railway" title="Portage railway">portage railway</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Don_Det%E2%80%93Don_Khon_railway" title="Don Det–Don Khon railway">Don Det–Don Khon narrow-gauge railway</a> built by the French in <a href="/wiki/Don_Det" title="Don Det">Don Det</a> and Don Khon in <a href="/wiki/Champasak_Province" title="Champasak Province">Champasak Province</a>. It has been closed since the 1940s. In the late 1920s, work began on the Thakhek–Tan Ap railway that would have run between <a href="/wiki/Thakhek" title="Thakhek">Thakhek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khammouane_Province" title="Khammouane Province">Khammouane Province</a> and <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A2n_%E1%BA%A4p_station" title="Tân Ấp station">Tân Ấp station</a> in Vietnam through the <a href="/wiki/M%E1%BB%A5_Gi%E1%BA%A1_Pass" title="Mụ Giạ Pass">Mụ Giạ Pass</a>. The scheme was aborted in the 1930s. Announced in 2015, a 414 kilometer high-speed rail line linking Kunming, in the southern Chinese province of Yunnan, with the Laotian capital of Vientiane is about 90% completed as of November 2020; the track is being laid, and the line is expected to be operational sometime in 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The major roads connecting the major urban centres, in particular <a href="/wiki/Route_13_(Laos)" title="Route 13 (Laos)">Route 13</a>, have been significantly upgraded in recent years, but villages far from major roads can be reached only through unpaved roads that may not be accessible year-round. </p>
      <p>There is limited external and internal telecommunication, but mobile phones have become widespread. Ninety-three percent of households have a telephone, either fixed line or mobile.<sup id="cite_ref-LSIS-II_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LSIS-II-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>8</span></sup> Electricity is available to 93% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-LSIS-II_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LSIS-II-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>8</span></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Songthaew" title="Songthaew">Songthaews</a></i> are used in the country for long-distance and local public transport. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply">Water supply</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Water supply">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Laos" title="Water supply and sanitation in Laos">Water supply and sanitation in Laos</a>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the World Bank data conducted in 2014, Laos has met the Millennium Development Goal (MDG) targets on water and sanitation regarding UNICEF/WHO Joint Monitoring Programme. However, as of 2018, there are approximately 1.9&nbsp;million Lao population could not access to improved water supply and 2.4&nbsp;million people without access to improved sanitation.<sup id="cite_ref-:8_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-135">[135]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Laos has made particularly noteworthy progress increasing access to <a href="/wiki/Sanitation" title="Sanitation">sanitation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-136">[136]</a></sup> Laos's predominantly rural<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> population makes investing in sanitation difficult. In 1990 only 8% of the rural population had access to improved sanitation.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-136">[136]</a></sup> Access rose rapidly from 10 percent in 1995 to 38 percent in 2008. Between 1995 and 2008 approximately 1,232,900 more people had access to improved sanitation in rural areas.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_136-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-136">[136]</a></sup> Laos's progress is notable in comparison to similar developing countries.<sup id="cite_ref-ODI1_136-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODI1-136">[136]</a></sup> The authorities in Laos have recently developed an innovative regulatory framework for public–private partnership contracts signed with small enterprises, in parallel with more conventional regulation of state-owned water enterprises.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Laos" title="Demographics of Laos">Demographics of Laos</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The term "Laotian" does not necessarily refer to the Lao language, ethnic Lao people, language or customs. It is a political term that includes the non-ethnic Lao groups within Laos and identifies them as "Laotian" because of their political citizenship. Laos has the youngest population of any country in Asia with a median age of 21.6 years.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-139">[139]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Laos's population was estimated at 7.45&nbsp;million in 2020, dispersed unevenly across the country. Most people live in valleys of the Mekong River and its tributaries. Vientiane prefecture, the capital and largest city, had about 683,000 residents in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-139">[139]</a></sup> </p> 
      <table class="navbox"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th colspan="10" class="navbox-title">

           </ul>
          </div> 
          <div style="height:2.6em;line-height:1.3em;">
           <span style="font-size:110%;">Largest cities or towns in Laos</span>
           <br>
