      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnicity">Ethnicity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Ethnicity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The people of Laos are often categorised by their distribution by <a href="/wiki/Elevation" title="Elevation">elevation</a>: (lowlands, midlands and upper high lands) as this somewhat correlates with ethnic groupings. More than half of the nation's population is ethnic Lao—the principal lowland inhabitants, and the politically and culturally dominant people of Laos.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_Demographic_Yearbooks_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_Demographic_Yearbooks-140">[140]</a></sup> The Lao belong to the <a href="/wiki/Tai_languages" title="Tai languages">Tai</a> linguistic group<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> who began migrating south from China in the first millennium CE.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> Ten percent belong to other "lowland" groups, which together with the Lao people make up the <a href="/wiki/Lao_Loum" title="Lao Loum">Lao Loum</a> (lowland people).<sup id="cite_ref-UN_Demographic_Yearbooks_140-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_Demographic_Yearbooks-140">[140]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the central and southern mountains, <a href="/wiki/Mon-Khmer" class="mw-redirect" title="Mon-Khmer">Mon-Khmer</a>-speaking groups, known as <a href="/wiki/Lao_Theung" title="Lao Theung">Lao Theung</a> or mid-slope Laotians, predominate. Other terms are Khmu, Khamu (Kammu) or Kha as the Lao Loum refer to them to indicate their <a href="/wiki/Austroasiatic" class="mw-redirect" title="Austroasiatic">Austroasiatic</a> language affiliation. However, the latter is considered pejorative, meaning 'slave'. They were the indigenous inhabitants of northern Laos. Some <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_people" title="Vietnamese people">Vietnamese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laotian_Chinese" title="Laotian Chinese">Laotian Chinese</a><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Thai_people" title="Thai people">Thai</a> minorities remain, particularly in the towns, but many left after independence in the late 1940s, many of whom relocated either to Vietnam, Hong Kong, or to France. Lao Theung constitute about 30% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Hill_people" title="Hill people">Hill people</a> and minority cultures of Laos such as the <a href="/wiki/Hmong_people" title="Hmong people">Hmong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yao_people" title="Yao people">Yao (Mien)</a> (<a href="/wiki/Hmong%E2%80%93Mien_languages" title="Hmong–Mien languages">Hmong-Mien</a>), <a href="/wiki/Yao_people" title="Yao people">Dao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shan_people" title="Shan people">Shan</a>, and several <a href="/wiki/Tibeto-Burman_languages" title="Tibeto-Burman languages">Tibeto-Burman</a> speaking peoples have lived in isolated regions of Laos for many years. Mountain/hill tribes of mixed ethno/cultural-linguistic heritage are found in northern Laos, which include the <a href="/wiki/Lua_people" title="Lua people">Lua</a> and <a href="/wiki/Khmu_people" title="Khmu people">Khmu people</a> who are indigenous to Laos. Collectively, they are known as <a href="/wiki/Lao_Sung" title="Lao Sung">Lao Soung</a> or highland Laotians. Lao Soung account for about 10% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica_45-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-45">[45]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The official and majority language is <a href="/wiki/Lao_language" title="Lao language">Lao</a>, a language of the <a href="/wiki/Tai_languages" title="Tai languages">Tai-Kadai</a> <a href="/wiki/Language_family" title="Language family">language family</a>. However, only slightly more than half of the population speaks Lao natively. The remainder, particularly in rural areas, speak ethnic minority languages. The <a href="/wiki/Lao_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="Lao alphabet">Lao alphabet</a>, which evolved sometime between the 13th and 14th centuries, was derived from the ancient <a href="/wiki/Khmer_script" title="Khmer script">Khmer script</a> and is very similar to Thai script.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> Languages like <a href="/wiki/Khmu_language" title="Khmu language">Khmu</a> (Austroasiatic) and <a href="/wiki/Hmong_language" title="Hmong language">Hmong</a> (<a href="/wiki/Hmong%E2%80%93Mien_languages" title="Hmong–Mien languages">Hmong-Mien</a>) are spoken by minorities, particularly in the midland and highland areas. A number of <a href="/wiki/Laotian_sign_languages" title="Laotian sign languages">Laotian sign languages</a> are used in areas with high rates of congenital deafness.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica_45-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-45">[45]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> is still commonly used in government and commerce. Over a third of Laos's students are educated through the medium of French, with French being compulsory for all other students. Throughout the country signage is bilingual in Lao and French, with French being predominant. Laos is a member of the French-speaking organisation of <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">La Francophonie</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, the language of the Association of Southeast Asian Nations (<a href="/wiki/ASEAN" title="ASEAN">ASEAN</a>), has become increasingly studied in recent years.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Laos" title="Religion in Laos">Religion in Laos</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Estupa_That_Luang.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Estupa_That_Luang.JPG/220px-Estupa_That_Luang.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Estupa_That_Luang.JPG/330px-Estupa_That_Luang.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Estupa_That_Luang.JPG/440px-Estupa_That_Luang.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3216" data-file-height="2136"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Estupa_That_Luang.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Pha_That_Luang" title="Pha That Luang">Pha That Luang</a> in Vientiane. The Buddhist <a href="/wiki/Stupa" title="Stupa">stupa</a> that is a national symbol of Laos.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Sixty-six percent of Laotians were <a href="/wiki/Theravada" title="Theravada">Theravada</a> <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhist</a>, 1.5 percent Christian, 0.1 percent Muslim, 0.1 percent Jewish, and 32.3 percent were other or traditional (mostly practitioners of <a href="/wiki/Tai_folk_religion" title="Tai folk religion">Satsana Phi</a>) in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-148">[148]</a></sup> Buddhism has long been one of the most important social forces in Laos. Theravada Buddhism has coexisted peacefully since its introduction to the country with the <a href="/wiki/Satsana_Phi" class="mw-redirect" title="Satsana Phi">local polytheism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica_45-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-45">[45]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Laos" title="Health in Laos">Health in Laos</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:VientianeHospital.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/VientianeHospital.jpg/220px-VientianeHospital.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/VientianeHospital.jpg/330px-VientianeHospital.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/VientianeHospital.jpg/440px-VientianeHospital.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3647" data-file-height="2403"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:VientianeHospital.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Mahosot_Hospital" title="Mahosot Hospital">Mahosot Hospital</a> in Vientiane.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Male <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy_at_birth" class="mw-redirect" title="Life expectancy at birth">life expectancy at birth</a> was at 62.6 years and female life expectancy was at 66.7 years in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-148">[148]</a></sup> Healthy life expectancy was 54 years in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-149">[149]</a></sup> Government expenditure on health is about four percent of GDP,<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-149">[149]</a></sup> about US$18 (PPP) in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_149-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-149">[149]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Laos" title="Education in Laos">Education in Laos</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/National_Library_of_Laos" title="National Library of Laos">National Library of Laos</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:National_University_of_Laos(NUOL)%E0%BA%A1.%E0%BA%8A_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/National_University_of_Laos%28NUOL%29%E0%BA%A1.%E0%BA%8A_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-National_University_of_Laos%28NUOL%29%E0%BA%A1.%E0%BA%8A_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/National_University_of_Laos%28NUOL%29%E0%BA%A1.%E0%BA%8A_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-National_University_of_Laos%28NUOL%29%E0%BA%A1.%E0%BA%8A_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/National_University_of_Laos%28NUOL%29%E0%BA%A1.%E0%BA%8A_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-National_University_of_Laos%28NUOL%29%E0%BA%A1.%E0%BA%8A_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:National_University_of_Laos(NUOL)%E0%BA%A1.%E0%BA%8A_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Laos" title="National University of Laos">National University of Laos</a> in Vientiane.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The adult <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a> rate for women in 2017 was 62.9%; for adult men, 78.1%.<sup id="cite_ref-LSIS-II_134-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LSIS-II-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>39–40</span></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2004 the net primary enrollment rate was 84%.<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_149-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-149">[149]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Laos" title="National University of Laos">National University of Laos</a> is the Lao state's public university. As a low-income country, Laos faces a <a href="/wiki/Brain-drain" class="mw-redirect" title="Brain-drain">brain-drain</a> problem as many educated people migrate to developed countries. It is estimated that about 37% of educated Laotians live outside Laos.<sup id="cite_ref-TonyFielding_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TonyFielding-150">[150]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Laos" title="Culture of Laos">Culture of Laos</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Lao_art" title="Lao art">Lao art</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lao_cuisine" title="Lao cuisine">Lao cuisine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dance_and_theatre_of_Laos" title="Dance and theatre of Laos">Dance and theatre of Laos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laotian_society" title="Laotian society">Laotian society</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_festivals_in_Laos" title="List of festivals in Laos">List of festivals in Laos</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Laos" title="Music of Laos">Music of Laos</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:3_Nagas_Feast.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/3_Nagas_Feast.jpg/220px-3_Nagas_Feast.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/3_Nagas_Feast.jpg/330px-3_Nagas_Feast.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/3_Nagas_Feast.jpg/440px-3_Nagas_Feast.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:3_Nagas_Feast.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An example of <a href="/wiki/Lao_cuisine" title="Lao cuisine">Lao cuisine</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Phuan_Girls.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Phuan_Girls.JPG/220px-Phuan_Girls.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="331" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Phuan_Girls.JPG/330px-Phuan_Girls.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Phuan_Girls.JPG/440px-Phuan_Girls.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1488" data-file-height="2240"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Phuan_Girls.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Lao women wearing <i><a href="/wiki/Sinh_(clothing)" title="Sinh (clothing)">sinhs</a></i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lao_New_Year,_dancers.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Lao_New_Year%2C_dancers.jpg/220px-Lao_New_Year%2C_dancers.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Lao_New_Year%2C_dancers.jpg/330px-Lao_New_Year%2C_dancers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Lao_New_Year%2C_dancers.jpg/440px-Lao_New_Year%2C_dancers.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lao_New_Year,_dancers.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Lao dancers during the <a href="/wiki/New_Year" title="New Year">New Year</a> celebration
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Theravada Buddhism is a dominant influence in Lao culture. It is evident throughout the country, expressed in language, temples and the arts and literature. Many elements of Lao culture predate Buddhism. For example, Laotian music is dominated by its national musical instrument, the <i><a href="/wiki/Khene" title="Khene">khaen</a></i>, a type of bamboo <a href="/wiki/Pan_flute" title="Pan flute">mouth organ</a> that has prehistoric origins. The <i>khaen</i> traditionally accompanied the singer in <i><a href="/wiki/Mor_lam" title="Mor lam">mor lam</a></i>, the dominant style of <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk music</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Glutinous_rice" title="Glutinous rice">Sticky rice</a> is a staple food and has cultural and religious significance to the Lao people. Sticky rice is generally preferred over <a href="/wiki/Jasmine_rice" title="Jasmine rice">jasmine rice</a>, and sticky rice cultivation and production is thought to have originated in Laos. There are many traditions and rituals associated with rice production in different environments and among many ethnic groups. For example, Khammu farmers in Luang Prabang plant the rice variety <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khao_kam&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Khao kam (page does not exist)">khao kam</a></i> in small quantities near the farm house in memory of dead parents, or at the edge of the rice field to indicate that parents are still alive.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Sinh_(clothing)" title="Sinh (clothing)">sinh</a></i> is a traditional garment worn by Lao women in daily life. It is a hand-woven silk skirt that can identify the woman who wears it in a variety of ways. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Laos" title="Cinema of Laos">Cinema of Laos</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Since the founding of the Lao PDR in 1975, very few films have been made in Laos.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> The first feature-length film made after the monarchy was abolished is <i>Gun Voice from the Plain of Jars</i>, directed by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Somchith_Pholsena&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Somchith Pholsena (page does not exist)">Somchith Pholsena</a> in 1983, although its release was prevented by a censorship board.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> One of the first commercial feature-length films was <i><a href="/wiki/Sabaidee_Luang_Prabang" title="Sabaidee Luang Prabang">Sabaidee Luang Prabang</a></i>, made in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> The 2017 documentary feature film <a href="/wiki/Blood_Road_(film)" title="Blood Road (film)">Blood Road</a> was predominantly shot and produced in Laos with assistance from the Lao government, it was recognized with a <a href="/wiki/News_%26_Documentary_Emmy_Award" title="News &amp; Documentary Emmy Award">News and Documentary Emmy Award</a> in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Australian filmmaker Kim Mordount's first feature film was made in Laos and features a Laotian cast speaking their native language. Entitled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Rocket_(2013_film)" title="The Rocket (2013 film)">The Rocket</a></i>, the film appeared at the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_International_Film_Festival" title="Melbourne International Film Festival">Melbourne International Film Festival</a> and won three awards at the Berlin International Film Festival.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> One production company's film that has succeeded to produce Lao feature films and gain international recognition is Lao New Wave Cinema's <i>At the Horizon</i>, directed by Anysay Keola, that was screened at the OzAsia Film Festival<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> and Lao Art Media's <i><a href="/wiki/Chanthaly" title="Chanthaly">Chanthaly</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Lao_language" title="Lao language">Lao</a>: ຈັນທະລີ) directed by <a href="/wiki/Mattie_Do" title="Mattie Do">Mattie Do</a>, which was screened at the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Fantastic_Fest" title="Fantastic Fest">Fantastic Fest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> In September 2017, Laos submitted <i><a href="/wiki/Dearest_Sister" title="Dearest Sister">Dearest Sister</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Lao_language" title="Lao language">Lao</a>: ນ້ອງຮັກ), Mattie Do's second feature film, to the <a href="/wiki/90th_Academy_Awards" title="90th Academy Awards">90th Academy Awards</a> (or the Oscars) for consideration for <a href="/wiki/List_of_submissions_to_the_90th_Academy_Awards_for_Best_Foreign_Language_Film" title="List of submissions to the 90th Academy Awards for Best Foreign Language Film">Best Foreign Language Film</a>, marking the country's first submission for the Oscars.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2018, Laos has three operating theatres dedicated to showing films.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">Festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>There are some public holidays, festivities and ceremonies in Laos. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Hmong New Year (Nopejao)</li> 
       <li>Bun Pha Wet</li> 
       <li>Magha Puja</li> 
       <li>Chinese New Year</li> 
       <li>Boun Khoun Khao</li> 
       <li>Boun Pimai</li> 
       <li>Visakha Puja</li> 
       <li>Pi Mai/Songkran(Lao New Year)</li> 
       <li>Khao Phansaa</li> 
       <li>Haw Khao Padap Din</li> 
       <li>Awk Phansaa</li> 
       <li>Bun Nam</li> 
       <li>Lao National Day (2 December)<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>All newspapers are published by the government, including two foreign language papers: the English-language daily <i><a href="/wiki/Vientiane_Times" title="Vientiane Times">Vientiane Times</a></i> and the French-language weekly <i><a href="/wiki/Le_R%C3%A9novateur" title="Le Rénovateur">Le Rénovateur</a></i>. Additionally, the Khao San Pathet Lao, the country's official news agency, publishes English and French versions of its eponymous paper. Laos has nine daily newspapers, 90 magazines, 43 radio stations, and 32 TV stations operating throughout the country. As of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, <i><a href="/wiki/Nh%C3%A2n_D%C3%A2n" title="Nhân Dân">Nhân Dân</a></i> ('The People') and the <a href="/wiki/Xinhua_News_Agency" title="Xinhua News Agency">Xinhua News Agency</a> are the only foreign media organisations permitted to open offices in Laos—both opened bureaus in Vientiane in 2011.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The Lao government controls all media channels to prevent critique of its actions.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> Lao citizens who have criticised the government have been subjected to enforced disappearances, arbitrary arrests and torture.<sup id="cite_ref-state_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-165">[165]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-atimes_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atimes-166">[166]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Polygamy">Polygamy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Polygamy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Polygamy" title="Polygamy">Polygamy</a> is officially a crime in Laos, though the penalty is minor. The constitution and Family Code bar the legal recognition of polygamous marriages, stipulating that <a href="/wiki/Monogamy" title="Monogamy">monogamy</a> is the principal form of marriage in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> Polygamy, however, is still customary among some Hmong people.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> Only 3.5% of women and 2.1% of men between the ages of 15–49 were in a polygynous union as of 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-LSIS-II_134-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LSIS-II-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>19</span></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Stadenat-vientiane.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Stadenat-vientiane.jpg/220px-Stadenat-vientiane.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="118" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Stadenat-vientiane.jpg/330px-Stadenat-vientiane.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Stadenat-vientiane.jpg/440px-Stadenat-vientiane.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1100"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Stadenat-vientiane.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/New_Laos_National_Stadium" title="New Laos National Stadium">New Laos National Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vientiane" title="Vientiane">Vientiane</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The martial art of <a href="/wiki/Muay_Lao" title="Muay Lao">muay Lao</a>, the national sport,<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> is a form of kickboxing similar to Thailand's <a href="/wiki/Muay_Thai" title="Muay Thai">muay Thai</a>, Burmese <a href="/wiki/Lethwei" title="Lethwei">Lethwei</a> and Cambodian <a href="/wiki/Pradal_Serey" class="mw-redirect" title="Pradal Serey">Pradal Serey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Association football</a> is the most popular sport in Laos.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Lao_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Lao League">Lao League</a> is the top professional league for association football clubs in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Lao_Premier_League_Website_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lao_Premier_League_Website-172">[172]</a></sup> Since the start of the league, <a href="/wiki/Lao_Army_F.C." title="Lao Army F.C.">Lao Army F.C.</a> has been the most successful club with 8 titles, the highest number of championship wins.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Laos has no tradition in other team sports. In 2017, the country sent a team for the first time to the team events at the <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asian_Games" title="Southeast Asian Games">Southeast Asian Games</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Laos_men%27s_national_basketball_team" title="Laos men's national basketball team">national basketball team</a> competed at the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_at_the_2017_Southeast_Asian_Games_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament" title="Basketball at the 2017 Southeast Asian Games – Men's tournament">2017 Southeast Asian Games</a> where it beat <a href="/wiki/Myanmar_men%27s_national_basketball_team" title="Myanmar men's national basketball team">Myanmar</a> in the eighth place game.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Laos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
